1. Text Quality: Output (a) is not as clear as Output (b). Output (a) uses "77°F" which is not a standard format for expressing temperature in Fahrenheit. The correct format should be "59.0° Fahrenheit" as in Output (b). Therefore, Output (b) has better Text Quality. 2. Information Richness: Both outputs provide the exact conversion of 15 degrees Celsius to Fahrenheit, which is sufficient for the given instruction. There is no additional information or examples provided in either output. Therefore, the Information Richness of both outputs is equal. 3. User Intention Inference: Neither output requires any inference about the user's intention as the instruction is clear and direct. Therefore, both outputs pass this criterion equally. 4. Accuracy: Both outputs are accurate as they correctly convert 15 degrees Celsius to Fahrenheit. The formula to convert Celsius to Fahrenheit is (Celsius * 9/5) + 32. So, (15 * 9/5) + 32 = 59 + 32 = 91, which is equivalent to 59.0° Fahrenheit. Therefore, both outputs are equally accurate. 5. Completeness of Instruction Following: Both outputs precisely follow the instruction by providing the exact conversion of the given temperature. There is no omission of any key instruction or explicit constraint. Therefore, both outputs are equally complete in following the instruction.  Overall, while both outputs are accurate and complete in following the instruction, Output (b) has a better Text Quality due to the correct format of expressing the temperature in Fahrenheit. Therefore, Output (b) is better.
